<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the U.S. territory. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_(disambiguation)" title="Puerto Rico (disambiguation)">Puerto Rico (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Porto Rico" and "Borinquen" redirect here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Porto_Rico_(disambiguation)" title="Porto Rico (disambiguation)">Porto Rico (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Borinquen_(disambiguation)" title="Borinquen (disambiguation)">Borinquen (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">
<li value="1"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_natlanthem"><b><a href="#ref_natlanthem">^</a></b></span> "The Star-Spangled Banner" serves as the national anthem for the United States of America and its territories.</li>
<li value="2"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_govtype"><b><a href="#ref_govtype">^</a></b></span> The term 'Commonwealth' does not describe or provide for any specific political status or relationship. It has, for example, been applied to both states and territories. When used in connection with areas under U.S. sovereignty that are not states, the term broadly describes an area that has a constitution of its adoption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
</ol>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Puerto Rico</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[a]</a></sup> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Language" title="Spanish Language">Spanish</a> for "Rich Port"), officially the <b>Commonwealth of Puerto Rico</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i><b>Estado Libre Asociado de Puerto Rico</b></i></span>, <abbr title="literally">lit.</abbr> "Free Associated State of Puerto Rico")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[b]</a></sup> and briefly called <b>Porto Rico</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[c]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_territories_of_the_United_States" title="Unincorporated territories of the United States">unincorporated territory</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> located in the northeast <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.</p>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a>, Puerto Rico includes the main island of Puerto Rico and a number of smaller ones, such as <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Mona" title="Isla de Mona">Mona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">Vieques</a>. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_capitals_in_the_United_States" title="List of capitals in the United States">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">most populous city</a> is <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>. Its official languages are <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, though Spanish predominates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup> The island's population is approximately 3.4 million. Puerto Rico's rich history, tropical climate, diverse natural scenery, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_cuisine" title="Puerto Rican cuisine">traditional cuisine</a>, and attractive <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Taxation in Puerto Rico">tax incentives</a> make it a popular destination for travelers from around the world.</p>
<p>Originally populated by the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> people, the island was claimed in 1493 by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a> during his second voyage. Later it endured invasion attempts from the French, Dutch, and British. Four centuries of Spanish colonial government transformed the island's ethnic, cultural and physical landscapes primarily with waves of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Spanish_New_World_colonies" title="Slavery in the Spanish New World colonies">African slaves</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canarian" title="Canarian">Canarian</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andalusian_people" title="Andalusian people">Andalusian</a> settlers. In the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish imperial</a> imagination, Puerto Rico played a secondary, but strategic role when compared to wealthier colonies like <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Peru</a> and the mainland parts of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup> Spain's distant administrative control continued up to the end of the 19th century, helping to produce a distinctive creole Hispanic culture and language that combined elements from the Native Americans, Africans, and Iberians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> In 1898, following the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> acquired Puerto Rico under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans" title="Puerto Ricans">Puerto Ricans</a> are by law <a href="/wiki/Birthright_citizenship_in_the_United_States" title="Birthright citizenship in the United States">natural-born citizens</a> of the United States and may move freely between the island and the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> As it is not a state Puerto Rico does not have a vote in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>, which governs the territory with full jurisdiction under the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Federal_Relations_Act_of_1950" title="Puerto Rico Federal Relations Act of 1950">Puerto Rico Federal Relations Act of 1950</a>. As a U.S. territory, American citizens residing on the island are <a href="/wiki/Federal_voting_rights_in_Puerto_Rico#Disenfranchisement_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Federal voting rights in Puerto Rico">disenfranchised at the national level</a> and do not <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">vote for president and vice president of the United States</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup> and do not pay federal income tax on Puerto Rican income. Congress approved <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Constitution of Puerto Rico">a local constitution</a>, allowing U.S. citizens on the territory to elect <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Governor of Puerto Rico">a governor</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_status_referendum,_2012" title="Puerto Rican status referendum, 2012">2012 referendum</a> showed a majority (54% of those who voted) disagreed with "the present form of territorial status". A second question asking about a new model, had full statehood the preferred option among those who voted for a change of status, although a significant number of people did not answer the second question of the referendum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup> Another <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_status_referendum,_2017" title="Puerto Rican status referendum, 2017">fifth referendum</a> was held on June 11, 2017, with "Statehood" and "Independence/Free Association" initially as the only available choices. At the recommendation of the Department of Justice, an option for the "current territorial status" was added.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup> The referendum showed an overwhelming support for statehood, with 97.18% voting for it, although the voter turnout had a historically low figure of only 22.99% of the registered voters casting their ballots.</p>
<p>In early 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_government-debt_crisis" title="Puerto Rican government-debt crisis">Puerto Rican government-debt crisis</a> posed serious problems for the government. The outstanding bond debt had climbed to $70 billion at a time with 12.4% unemployment. The debt had been increasing during a decade long recession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-30">[27]</a></sup> This was the second major financial crisis to affect the island after the Great Depression when the U.S. government, in 1935, provided relief efforts through the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Reconstruction_Administration" title="Puerto Rico Reconstruction Administration">Puerto Rico Reconstruction Administration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[28]</a></sup> On May 3, 2017, Puerto Rico's financial oversight board in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Puerto_Rico" title="United States District Court for the District of Puerto Rico">U.S. District Court for Puerto Rico</a> filed the debt restructuring petition which was made under Title III of <a href="/wiki/PROMESA" title="PROMESA">PROMESA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[29]</a></sup> By early August 2017, the debt was $72 billion with a 45% poverty rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters.com_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-33">[30]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>Puerto Rico means "rich port" in Spanish. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" title="Puerto Rican people">Puerto Ricans</a> often call the island <i><span lang="es">Borinquén</span></i> – a derivation of <i><span lang="tnq">Borikén</span></i>, its <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> name, which means "Land of the Valiant Lord".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup> The terms <i><span lang="es">boricua</span></i> and <i><span lang="es">borincano</span></i> derive from <i><span lang="tnq">Borikén</span></i> and <i><span lang="tnq">Borinquen</span></i> respectively, and are commonly used to identify someone of Puerto Rican heritage. The island is also popularly known in Spanish as <i><span lang="es">la isla del encanto</span></i>, meaning "the island of enchantment".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Columbus named the island <i><span lang="es">San Juan Bautista</span></i>, in honor of Saint <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John the Baptist</a>, while the capital city was named <i><span lang="es">Ciudad de Puerto Rico</span></i> ("Rich Port City"). Eventually traders and other maritime visitors came to refer to the entire island as Puerto Rico, while San Juan became the name used for the main trading/shipping port and the capital city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[d]</a></sup></p>
<p>The island's name was changed to "Porto Rico" by the United States after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[36]</a></sup> The anglicized name was used by the US government and private enterprises. The name was changed back to Puerto Rico by a joint resolution in Congress introduced by <span lang="es"><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_C%C3%B3rdova_D%C3%A1vila" title="Félix Córdova Dávila">Félix Córdova Dávila</a></span> in 1931.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The official name of the entity in Spanish is <i><span lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Estado_Libre_Asociado_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Estado Libre Asociado de Puerto Rico">Estado Libre Asociado de Puerto Rico</a></span></i> ("free <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">associated state</a> of Puerto Rico"), while its official English name is <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._insular_area)#Commonwealth_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Commonwealth (U.S. insular area)">Commonwealth of Puerto Rico</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Puerto_Rico" title="History of Puerto Rico">History of Puerto Rico</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_era">Pre-Columbian era</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taino_Village.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Taino_Village.JPG/250px-Taino_Village.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Taino_Village.JPG/375px-Taino_Village.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Taino_Village.JPG/500px-Taino_Village.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taino_Village.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A reconstructed Taíno village at the <a href="/wiki/Tibes_Indigenous_Ceremonial_Center" title="Tibes Indigenous Ceremonial Center">Tibes Ceremonial Center</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The ancient history of the archipelago which is now Puerto Rico is not well known. Unlike other indigenous cultures in the New World (<a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztec</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayan_civilization" title="Mayan civilization">Maya</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inca" title="Inca">Inca</a>) which left behind abundant archeological and physical evidence of their societies, scant artifacts and evidence remain of the Puerto Rico's indigenous population. Scarce archaeological findings and early Spanish accounts from the colonial era constitute all that is known about them. The first comprehensive book on the history of Puerto Rico was written by <a href="/wiki/Fray_%C3%8D%C3%B1igo_Abbad_y_Lasierra" title="Fray Íñigo Abbad y Lasierra">Fray Íñigo Abbad y Lasierra</a> in 1786, nearly three centuries after the first Spaniards landed on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first known settlers were the <a href="/wiki/Ortoiroid_people" title="Ortoiroid people">Ortoiroid people</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaic_period_in_the_Americas" title="Archaic period in the Americas">Archaic Period</a> culture of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Amerindian</a> hunters and fishermen who migrated from the South American mainland. Some scholars suggest their settlement dates back about 4,000 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rouse_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rouse-43">[39]</a></sup> An archeological dig in 1990 on the island of <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">Vieques</a> found the remains of a man, designated as the "Puerto Ferro Man", which was dated to around 2000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[40]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ortoiroid_people" title="Ortoiroid people">Ortoiroid</a> were displaced by the <a href="/wiki/Saladoid" title="Saladoid">Saladoid</a>, a culture from the same region that arrived on the island between 430 and 250 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rouse_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rouse-43">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Igneri" title="Igneri">Igneri</a> tribe migrated to Puerto Rico between 120 and 400 AD from the region of the <a href="/wiki/Orinoco" title="Orinoco">Orinoco</a> river in northern South America. The Arcaico and Igneri co-existed on the island between the 4th and 10th centuries.</p>
<p>Between the 7th and 11th centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> culture developed on the island. By approximately 1000 AD, it had become dominant. At the time of Columbus' arrival, an estimated 30,000 to 60,000 Taíno Amerindians, led by the <i><a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a></i> (chief) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ag%C3%BCeyban%C3%A1_(The_Great_Sun)" title="Agüeybaná (The Great Sun)">Agüeybaná</a>, inhabited the island. They called it <i>Boriken</i>, meaning "the great land of the valiant and noble Lord".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[41]</a></sup> The natives lived in small villages, each led by a cacique. They subsisted by hunting and fishing, done generally by men, as well as by the women's gathering and processing of indigenous <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> root and fruit. This lasted until Columbus arrived in 1493.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Spanish_colony_(1493–1898)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_colony_.281493.E2.80.931898.29">Spanish colony (1493–1898)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Captaincy General of Puerto Rico">Captaincy General of Puerto Rico</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RUIDIAZ(1893)_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1325" data-file-width="1019" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg/150px-RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg/225px-RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg/300px-RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RUIDIAZ(1893)_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de León">Juan Ponce de León</a> (<a href="/wiki/Santerv%C3%A1s_de_Campos" title="Santervás de Campos">Santervás de Campos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Valladolid" title="Province of Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, Spain), Puerto Rico's first governor</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_and_early_settlement">Conquest and early settlement</span></h4>
<p>When Columbus arrived in Puerto Rico during his second voyage on November 19, 1493, the island was inhabited by the Taíno. They called it <i>Borikén</i> (<i>Borinquen</i> in Spanish transliteration). Columbus named the island San Juan Bautista, in honor of St <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John the Baptist</a>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[e]</a></sup> Having reported the findings of his first travel, Columbus brought with him this time a letter from King Ferdinand<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[44]</a></sup> empowered by a <a href="/wiki/Inter_caetera" title="Inter caetera">papal bull</a> that authorized any course of action necessary for the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and the Christian faith. <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de León">Juan Ponce de León</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant" title="Lieutenant">lieutenant</a> under Columbus, founded the first Spanish settlement, <a href="/wiki/Caparra_Archaeological_Site" title="Caparra Archaeological Site">Caparra</a>, on August 8, 1508. He later served as the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Puerto_Rico" title="List of Governors of Puerto Rico">governor</a> of the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[f]</a></sup> Eventually, traders and other maritime visitors came to refer to the entire island as Puerto Rico, and San Juan became the name of the main trading/shipping port.</p>
<p>At the beginning of the 16th century, the Spanish people began to colonize the island. Despite the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_Burgos" title="Laws of Burgos">Laws of Burgos</a> of 1512 and other decrees for the protection of the indigenous population, some Taíno Indians were forced into an <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomienda</a> system of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Spanish_New_World_colonies" title="Slavery in the Spanish New World colonies">forced labor</a> in the early years of colonization. The population suffered extremely high fatalities from epidemics of European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious" title="Infectious">infectious</a> diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[g]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[h]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[i]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[j]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[k]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Colonization,_the_Habsburgs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonization.2C_the_Habsburgs">Colonization, the Habsburgs</span></h4>
<p>In 1520, <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">King Charles I of Spain</a> issued a royal decree collectively emancipating the remaining Taíno population. By that time, the Taíno people were few in number.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[52]</a></sup> Enslaved Africans had already begun to compensate for the native labor loss, but their numbers were proportionate to the diminished commercial interest Spain soon began to demonstrate for the island colony. Other nearby islands, like Cuba, Saint-Domingue, and Guadeloupe, attracted more of the slave trade than Puerto Rico, probably because of greater agricultural interests in those islands, on which colonists had developed large sugar plantations and had the capital to invest in the Atlantic slave trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stark_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stark-64">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the beginning of the country, the colonial administration relied heavily on the industry of enslaved Africans and creole blacks for public works and defenses, primarily in coastal ports and cities, where the tiny colonial population had hunkered down. With no significant industries or large-scale agricultural production as yet, enslaved and free communities lodged around the few littoral settlements, particularly around San Juan, also forming lasting Afro-creole communities. Meanwhile, in the island's interior, there developed a mixed and independent peasantry that relied on a subsistence economy. This mostly unsupervised population supplied villages and settlements with foodstuffs and, in relative isolation, set the pattern for what later would be known as the <a href="/wiki/J%C3%ADbaro" title="Jíbaro">Puerto Rican Jíbaro culture</a>. By the end of the 16th Century, the Spanish Empire was diminishing and, in the face of increasing raids from European competitors, the colonial administration throughout <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">the Americas</a> fell into a "bunker mentality". Imperial strategists and urban planners redesigned port settlements into military posts with the objective of protecting Spanish territorial claims and ensuring the safe passing of the king's silver-laden <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">Atlantic Fleet</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>. San Juan served as an important port-of-call for ships driven across the Atlantic by its powerful <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean#Climate" title="Atlantic Ocean">trade winds</a>. West Indies convoys linked Spain to the island, sailing between <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> and the Spanish West Indies. The colony's seat of government was on the forested <a href="/wiki/Isleta_de_San_Juan" title="Isleta de San Juan">Islet of San Juan</a> and for a time became one of the most heavily fortified settlements in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_West_Indies" title="Spanish West Indies">Spanish Caribbean</a> earning the name of the "Walled City". The islet is still dotted with the various forts and walls, such as <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">Castillo San Felipe del Morro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Crist%C3%B3bal" title="Castillo San Cristóbal">Castillo San Cristóbal</a>, designed to protect the population and the strategic <a href="/wiki/Port_of_San_Juan" title="Port of San Juan">Port of San Juan</a> from the raids of the Spanish European competitors.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hendricksz_1625_attack_on_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="2688" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hendricksz_1625_attack_on_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/300px-Hendricksz_1625_attack_on_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hendricksz_1625_attack_on_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/450px-Hendricksz_1625_attack_on_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hendricksz_1625_attack_on_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/600px-Hendricksz_1625_attack_on_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hendricksz_1625_attack_on_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hendricksz 1625 attack on San Juan, Puerto Rico</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1625, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Juan_(1625)" title="Battle of San Juan (1625)">Battle of San Juan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> commander <a href="/wiki/Boudewijn_Hendricksz" title="Boudewijn Hendricksz">Boudewijn Hendricksz</a> tested the defenses' limits like no one else before. Learning from <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a>'s previous <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Juan_(1595)" title="Battle of San Juan (1595)">failures here</a>, he circumvented the cannons of the castle of San Felipe del Morro and quickly brought his 17 ships into the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Bay" title="San Juan Bay">San Juan Bay</a>. He then occupied the port and attacked the city while the population hurried for shelter behind the Morro's moat and high battlements. Historians consider this event the worst attack on San Juan. Though the Dutch set the village on fire, they failed to conquer the Morro, and its batteries pounded their troops and ships until Hendricksz deemed the cause lost. Hendricksz's expedition eventually helped propel a fortification frenzy. Constructions of defenses for the San Cristóbal Hill were soon ordered so as to prevent the landing of invaders out of reach of the Morro's artillery. Urban planning responded to the needs of keeping the colony in Spanish hands.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_colonial_period">Late colonial period</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hacienda_La_Fortuna_Francisco_Oller_1885_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="918" data-file-width="1536" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hacienda_La_Fortuna_Francisco_Oller_1885_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg/220px-Hacienda_La_Fortuna_Francisco_Oller_1885_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hacienda_La_Fortuna_Francisco_Oller_1885_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg/330px-Hacienda_La_Fortuna_Francisco_Oller_1885_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hacienda_La_Fortuna_Francisco_Oller_1885_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg/440px-Hacienda_La_Fortuna_Francisco_Oller_1885_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hacienda_La_Fortuna_Francisco_Oller_1885_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Hacienda La Fortuna</i>. A sugar mill complex in Puerto Rico painted by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Oller" title="Francisco Oller">Francisco Oller</a> in 1885 (<a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the late 16th and early 17th centuries, Spain concentrated its colonial efforts on the more prosperous mainland North, Central, and South American colonies. With the advent of the lively Bourbon Dynasty in Spain in the 1700s, the island of Puerto Rico began a gradual shift to more imperial attention. More roads began connecting previously isolated inland settlements to coastal cities, and coastal settlements like Arecibo, Mayaguez, and Ponce began acquiring importance of their own, separate from San Juan. By the end of the 18th century, merchant ships from an array of nationalities threatened the tight regulations of the Mercantilist system, which turned each colony solely toward the European metropole and limited contact with other nations. U.S. ships came to surpass Spanish trade and with this also came the exploitation of the island's natural resources. Slavers, which had made but few stops on the island before, began selling more enslaved Africans to growing sugar and coffee plantations. The increasing number of Atlantic wars in which the Caribbean islands played major roles, like the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Revolutions" title="Atlantic Revolutions">Atlantic Revolutions</a>, ensured Puerto Rico's growing esteem in Madrid's eyes. On April 17, 1797, Sir <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Abercromby" title="Ralph Abercromby">Ralph Abercromby</a> fleet invaded the island with a force of 6,000–13,000 men,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[54]</a></sup> which included German soldiers and Royal Marines and 60 to 64 ships. Fierce fighting continued for the next days with Spanish troops. Both sides suffered heavy losses. On Sunday April 30 the British ceased their attack and began their retreat from San Juan. By the time independence movements in the larger Spanish colonies gained success, new waves of loyal creole immigrants began to arrive in Puerto Rico, helping to tilt the island's political balance toward the Crown.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EAGLE_Old_San_Juan_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="854" data-file-width="1280" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/EAGLE_Old_San_Juan_2014.jpg/300px-EAGLE_Old_San_Juan_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/EAGLE_Old_San_Juan_2014.jpg/450px-EAGLE_Old_San_Juan_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/EAGLE_Old_San_Juan_2014.jpg/600px-EAGLE_Old_San_Juan_2014.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EAGLE_Old_San_Juan_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 16th-century fort, <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">Castillo San Felipe del Morro</a>, in San Juan, Puerto Rico</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1809, to secure its political bond with the island and in the midst of the European <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Junta_(Peninsular_War)" title="Junta (Peninsular War)">Supreme Central Junta</a> based in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> recognized Puerto Rico as an overseas province of Spain. This gave the island residents the right to elect representatives to the recently convened <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_Cortes" title="Cádiz Cortes">Spanish parliament</a> (Cádiz Cortes), with equal representation to mainland Iberian, Mediterranean (Balearic Islands) and Atlantic maritime Spanish provinces (Canary Islands).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Power_y_Giralt" title="Ramón Power y Giralt">Ramón Power y Giralt</a>, the first Spanish parliamentary representative from the island of Puerto Rico, died after serving a three-year term in the Cortes. These <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1812" title="Spanish Constitution of 1812">parliamentary and constitutional reforms</a> were in force from 1810 to 1814, and again from 1820 to 1823. They were twice reversed during the restoration of the traditional monarchy by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII</a>. Immigration and commercial trade reforms in the 19th century increased the island's ethnic European population and economy and expanded the Spanish cultural and social imprint on the local character of the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Minor slave revolts had occurred on the island throughout the years, with the revolt planned and organized by <a href="/wiki/Marcos_Xiorro" title="Marcos Xiorro">Marcos Xiorro</a> in 1821 being the most important. Even though the conspiracy was unsuccessful, Xiorro achieved legendary status and is part of Puerto Rico's folklore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GB_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-GB-66">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_of_liberalism">Politics of liberalism</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="363" data-file-width="510" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg/300px-Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg/450px-Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Intentona_de_Yauco.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The flag flown by Fidel Vélez and his men during the "Intentona de Yauco" revolt</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the early 19th century, Puerto Rico spawned an independence movement that, due to harsh persecution by the Spanish authorities, convened in the island of St. Thomas. The movement was largely inspired by the ideals of <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> in establishing a <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_New_Granada" title="United Provinces of New Granada">United Provinces of New Granada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, that included Puerto Rico and Cuba. Among the influential members of this movement were Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Valero_de_Bernab%C3%A9" title="Antonio Valero de Bernabé">Antonio Valero de Bernabé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_de_las_Mercedes_Barbudo" title="María de las Mercedes Barbudo">María de las Mercedes Barbudo</a>. The movement was discovered, and Governor <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_la_Torre" title="Miguel de la Torre">Miguel de la Torre</a> had its members imprisoned or exiled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the increasingly rapid growth of independent former Spanish colonies in the South and Central American states in the first part of the 19th century, the Spanish Crown considered Puerto Rico and Cuba of strategic importance. To increase its hold on its last two New World colonies, the Spanish Crown revived the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Decree_of_Graces_of_1815" title="Royal Decree of Graces of 1815">Royal Decree of Graces of 1815</a> as a result of which 450,000 immigrants, mainly Spaniards, settled on the island in the period up until the American conquest. Printed in three languages—Spanish, English, and French—it was intended to also attract non-Spanish Europeans, with the hope that the independence movements would lose their popularity if new settlers had stronger ties to the Crown. Hundreds of non Spanish families, mainly from <a href="/wiki/Corsican_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Corsican immigration to Puerto Rico">Corsica</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="French immigration to Puerto Rico">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="German immigration to Puerto Rico">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Irish immigration to Puerto Rico">Ireland</a>, Italy and Scotland, also immigrated to the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Graces_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Graces-68">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Free land was offered as an incentive to those who wanted to populate the two islands, on the condition that they swear their loyalty to the Spanish Crown and allegiance to the Roman Catholic Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Graces_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Graces-68">[57]</a></sup> The offer was very successful, and European immigration continued even after 1898. Puerto Rico still receives Spanish and European immigration.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LARESFLAG2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="109" data-file-width="120" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/96/LARESFLAG2.jpg" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LARESFLAG2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Lares Revolutionary Flag</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poverty and political estrangement with Spain led to a small but significant uprising in 1868 known as <i><a href="/wiki/Grito_de_Lares" title="Grito de Lares">Grito de Lares</a>.</i> It began in the rural town of Lares, but was subdued when rebels moved to the neighboring town of San Sebastián.</p>
<p>Leaders of this independence movement included <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Emeterio_Betances" title="Ramón Emeterio Betances">Ramón Emeterio Betances</a>, considered the "father" of the Puerto Rican independence movement, and other political figures such as <a href="/wiki/Segundo_Ruiz_Belvis" title="Segundo Ruiz Belvis">Segundo Ruiz Belvis</a>. Slavery was abolished in Puerto Rico in 1873, "with provisions for periods of apprenticeship".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[58]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IMG_2972_-_Abolition_Park_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1004" data-file-width="733" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/IMG_2972_-_Abolition_Park_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-IMG_2972_-_Abolition_Park_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/IMG_2972_-_Abolition_Park_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-IMG_2972_-_Abolition_Park_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/IMG_2972_-_Abolition_Park_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-IMG_2972_-_Abolition_Park_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IMG_2972_-_Abolition_Park_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Parque_de_la_Abolici%C3%B3n" title="Parque de la Abolición">Abolition Park</a> in Ponce, Puerto Rico</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Leaders of "El Grito de Lares" went into exile in New York City. Many joined the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Committee_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Revolutionary Committee of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rican Revolutionary Committee</a>, founded on December 8, 1895, and continued their quest for Puerto Rican independence. In 1897, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Mattei_Lluberas" title="Antonio Mattei Lluberas">Antonio Mattei Lluberas</a> and the local leaders of the independence movement in Yauco organized another uprising, which became known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Intentona_de_Yauco" title="Intentona de Yauco">Intentona de Yauco</a></i>. They raised what they called the Puerto Rican flag, which was adopted as the national flag. The local conservative political factions opposed independence. Rumors of the planned event spread to the local Spanish authorities who acted swiftly and put an end to what would be the last major uprising in the island to Spanish colonial rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HMPR_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-HMPR-70">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1897, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Rivera" title="Luis Muñoz Rivera">Luis Muñoz Rivera</a> and others persuaded the liberal Spanish government to agree to grant limited self-government to the island by <a href="/wiki/Decree" title="Decree">royal decree</a> in the Autonomic Charter, including a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral legislature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[60]</a></sup> In 1898, Puerto Rico's first, but short-lived, quasi-autonomous government was organized as an "overseas province" of Spain. This bilaterally agreed-upon charter maintained a governor appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">King of Spain</a> – who held the power to annul any legislative decision – and a partially elected parliamentary structure. In February, Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Mac%C3%ADas_y_Casado" title="Manuel Macías y Casado">Manuel Macías</a> inaugurated the new government under the Autonomic Charter. General elections were held in March and the new government began to function on July 17, 1898.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="American_era_(1898–present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="American_era_.281898.E2.80.93present.29">American era (1898–present)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Campaign" title="Puerto Rican Campaign">Puerto Rican Campaign</a></div>
<p>In 1890, Captain <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Thayer_Mahan" title="Alfred Thayer Mahan">Alfred Thayer Mahan</a>, a member of the Navy War Board and leading U.S. strategic thinker, published a book titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Influence_of_Sea_Power_upon_History" title="The Influence of Sea Power upon History">The Influence of Sea Power upon History</a></i> in which he argued for the establishment of a large and powerful navy modeled after the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>. Part of his strategy called for the acquisition of colonies in the Caribbean, which would serve as coaling and naval stations. They would serve as strategic points of defense with the construction of a canal through the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a>, to allow easier passage of ships between the Atlantic and Pacific oceans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-SP-75">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_Company_of_native_Puerto_Ricans_in_the_American_Army.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="394" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/First_Company_of_native_Puerto_Ricans_in_the_American_Army.jpg/220px-First_Company_of_native_Puerto_Ricans_in_the_American_Army.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/First_Company_of_native_Puerto_Ricans_in_the_American_Army.jpg/330px-First_Company_of_native_Puerto_Ricans_in_the_American_Army.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1e/First_Company_of_native_Puerto_Ricans_in_the_American_Army.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_Company_of_native_Puerto_Ricans_in_the_American_Army.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first company of Puerto Ricans enlisted in the U.S. Army, 1899</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/William_H._Seward" title="William H. Seward">William H. Seward</a>, the former Secretary of State under presidents <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnson" title="Andrew Johnson">Andrew Johnson</a>, had also stressed the importance of building a canal in <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> or <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>. He suggested that the United States annex the Dominican Republic and purchase Puerto Rico and Cuba. The U.S. Senate did not approve his annexation proposal, and Spain rejected the U.S. offer of <span class="nowrap">160 million</span> dollars for Puerto Rico and Cuba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-SP-75">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 1894, the United States <a href="/wiki/Naval_War_College" title="Naval War College">Naval War College</a> had been developing <a href="/wiki/Contingency_plan" title="Contingency plan">contingency plans</a> for a war with Spain. By 1896, the U.S. Office of Naval Intelligence had prepared a plan that included military operations in Puerto Rican waters. Except for one 1895 plan, which recommended annexation of the island then named <i>Isle of Pines</i> (later renamed as <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_la_Juventud" title="Isla de la Juventud">Isla de la Juventud</a>), a recommendation dropped in later planning, plans developed for attacks on Spanish territories were intended as support operations against Spain's forces in and around Cuba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[65]</a></sup> Recent research suggests that the U.S. did consider Puerto Rico valuable as a naval station, and recognized that it and Cuba generated lucrative crops of sugar – a valuable commercial commodity which the United States lacked,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[66]</a></sup> before the development of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_Beet" title="Sugar Beet">Sugar Beet</a> industry in the United States.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:267px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Children_in_a_company_housing_settlement,_Puerto_Rico_1a34030u.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3058" data-file-width="4438" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Children_in_a_company_housing_settlement%2C_Puerto_Rico_1a34030u.jpg/265px-Children_in_a_company_housing_settlement%2C_Puerto_Rico_1a34030u.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Children_in_a_company_housing_settlement%2C_Puerto_Rico_1a34030u.jpg/398px-Children_in_a_company_housing_settlement%2C_Puerto_Rico_1a34030u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Children_in_a_company_housing_settlement%2C_Puerto_Rico_1a34030u.jpg/530px-Children_in_a_company_housing_settlement%2C_Puerto_Rico_1a34030u.jpg 2x" width="265"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Children_in_a_company_housing_settlement,_Puerto_Rico_1a34030u.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Children in a company housing settlement, 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On July 25, 1898, during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, the U.S. invaded Puerto Rico with a landing at <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guánica, Puerto Rico">Guánica</a>. As an outcome of the war, Spain ceded Puerto Rico, along with the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, then under Spanish sovereignty, to the U.S. under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris</a>. Spain relinquished sovereignty over Cuba, but did not cede it to the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[67]</a></sup> Later, Cuba became nominally independent but effectively a US protectorate until its 1958 revolution.</p>
<h4><span id="United_States_unincorporated_organized_territory_(1900–1952)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_unincorporated_organized_territory_.281900.E2.80.931952.29">United States unincorporated organized territory (1900–1952)</span></h4>
<p>The United States and Puerto Rico began a long-standing metropolis-colony relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[68]</a></sup> In the early 20th century, Puerto Rico was ruled by the military, with officials including the governor appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Foraker_Act" title="Foraker Act">Foraker Act</a> of 1900 gave Puerto Rico a certain amount of civilian popular government, including a popularly elected House of Representatives. The upper house and governor were appointed by the United States.</p>
<p>Its judicial system was constructed to follow the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_United_States" title="Law of the United States">American legal system</a>; a <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Supreme Court of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico Supreme Court</a> and a <a href="/wiki/United_States_territorial_court" title="United States territorial court">United State District Court</a> for the territory were established. It was authorized a non-voting member of Congress, by the title of "Resident Commissioner", who was appointed. In addition, this Act extended all U.S. laws "not locally inapplicable" to Puerto Rico, specifying, in particular, exemption from U.S. Internal Revenue laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-status-80">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Act empowered the civil government to legislate on "all matters of legislative character not locally inapplicable", including the power to modify and repeal any laws then in existence in Puerto Rico, though the U.S. Congress retained the power to annul acts of the Puerto Rico legislature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-status-80">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[70]</a></sup> During an address to the Puerto Rican legislature in 1906, President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> recommended that Puerto Ricans become U.S. citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-status-80">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1914, the Puerto Rican House of Delegates voted unanimously in favor of independence from the United States, but this was rejected by the U.S. Congress as "unconstitutional", and in violation of the 1900 <a href="/wiki/Foraker_Act" title="Foraker Act">Foraker Act</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gonzalez_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gonzalez-83">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._citizenship_and_Puerto_Rican_citizenship"><b>U.S. citizenship and Puerto Rican citizenship</b></span></h5>
<p>In 1917, the U.S. Congress passed the <a href="/wiki/Jones%E2%80%93Shafroth_Act" title="Jones–Shafroth Act">Jones–Shafroth Act</a>, popularly called the Jones Act, which granted Puerto Ricans, born on or after, April 25, 1898, U.S. citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[73]</a></sup> Opponents, which included all of the Puerto Rican House of Delegates, who voted unanimously against it, said that the US imposed citizenship in order to draft Puerto Rican men into the army as American entry into <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> became likely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gonzalez_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gonzalez-83">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The same Act provided for a popularly elected Senate to complete a bicameral Legislative Assembly, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Bill_of_rights" title="Bill of rights">bill of rights</a>. It authorized the popular election of the Resident Commissioner to a four-year term.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Ricans_in_WWII.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="244" data-file-width="300" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Puerto_Ricans_in_WWII.jpg/220px-Puerto_Ricans_in_WWII.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/Puerto_Ricans_in_WWII.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Ricans_in_WWII.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/65th_Infantry_Regiment_(United_States)" title="65th Infantry Regiment (United States)">65th Infantry</a> training in Salinas, Puerto Rico (August 1941)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Natural disasters, including a major <a href="/wiki/1918_San_Ferm%C3%ADn_earthquake" title="1918 San Fermín earthquake">earthquake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> in 1918, and several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">hurricanes</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> impoverished the island during the first few decades under U.S. rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[74]</a></sup> Some political leaders, such as <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Albizu_Campos" title="Pedro Albizu Campos">Pedro Albizu Campos</a>, who led the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Nationalist_Party" title="Puerto Rican Nationalist Party">Puerto Rican Nationalist Party</a>, demanded change in relations with the United States. He organized a protest at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico,_R%C3%ADo_Piedras_Campus" title="University of Puerto Rico, Río Piedras Campus">University of Puerto Rico</a> in 1935, in which <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras_massacre" title="Río Piedras massacre">four were killed</a> by police.</p>
<p>In 1936, U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Millard_Tydings" title="Millard Tydings">Millard Tydings</a> introduced a bill supporting independence for Puerto Rico, but it was opposed by <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn" title="Luis Muñoz Marín">Luis Muñoz Marín</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Liberal Party of Puerto Rico">Liberal Party of Puerto Rico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gatell_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gatell-86">[75]</a></sup> (Tydings had co-sponsored the <a href="/wiki/Tydings%E2%80%93McDuffie_Act" title="Tydings–McDuffie Act">Tydings–McDuffie Act</a>, which provided independence to the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> after a 10-year transition under a limited autonomy.) All the Puerto Rican parties supported the bill, but Muñoz Marín opposed it. Tydings did not gain passage of the bill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gatell_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gatell-86">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1937, Albizu Campos' party organized a protest in which numerous people were killed by police in <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>. The Insular Police, resembling the <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" title="National Guard of the United States">National Guard</a>, opened fire upon unarmed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1937inquiry_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-1937inquiry-87">[76]</a></sup> cadets and bystanders alike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1937inquiry_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-1937inquiry-87">[76]</a></sup> The attack on unarmed protesters was reported by the U.S. Congressman <a href="/wiki/Vito_Marcantonio" title="Vito Marcantonio">Vito Marcantonio</a> and confirmed by the report of the Hays Commission, which investigated the events. The commission was led by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Garfield_Hays" title="Arthur Garfield Hays">Arthur Garfield Hays</a>, counsel to the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Liberties_Union" title="American Civil Liberties Union">American Civil Liberties Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1937inquiry_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-1937inquiry-87">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nineteen people were killed and over 200 were badly wounded, many in their backs while running away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5yrs_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-5yrs-88">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[78]</a></sup> The Hays Commission declared it a <a href="/wiki/List_of_events_named_massacres" title="List of events named massacres">massacre</a> and police mob action,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5yrs_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-5yrs-88">[77]</a></sup> and it has since been known as the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_massacre" title="Ponce massacre">Ponce massacre</a>. In the aftermath, on April 2, 1943, Tydings introduced a bill in Congress calling for independence for Puerto Rico. This bill ultimately was defeated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_80-3"><a href="#cite_note-status-80">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the latter years of the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Roosevelt</a>–<a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Truman</a> administrations, the internal governance was changed in a compromise reached with Luis Muñoz Marín and other Puerto Rican leaders. In 1946, President Truman appointed the first Puerto Rican-born governor, <a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_T._Pi%C3%B1ero" title="Jesús T. Piñero">Jesús T. Piñero</a>.</p>
<p>Since 2007, the Puerto Rico State Department has developed a protocol to issue certificates of Puerto Rican citizenship to Puerto Ricans. In order to be eligible, applicants must have been born in Puerto Rico; born outside of Puerto Rico to a Puerto Rican–born parent; or be an American citizen with at least one year of residence in Puerto Rico.</p>
<h4><span id="United_States_unincorporated_organized_territory_with_commonwealth_constitution_(1952–present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_unincorporated_organized_territory_with_commonwealth_constitution_.281952.E2.80.93present.29">United States unincorporated organized territory with commonwealth constitution (1952–present)</span></h4>
<p>In 1947, the U.S. granted Puerto Ricans the right to democratically elect their own <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Governor of Puerto Rico">governor</a>. In 1948, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn" title="Luis Muñoz Marín">Luis Muñoz Marín</a> became the first popularly elected governor of Puerto Rico.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_65th_Infantry_Regiment.Painting.Korean_War.Bayonet_charge_against_Chinese_division.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4694" data-file-width="6335" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/US_65th_Infantry_Regiment.Painting.Korean_War.Bayonet_charge_against_Chinese_division.jpg/280px-US_65th_Infantry_Regiment.Painting.Korean_War.Bayonet_charge_against_Chinese_division.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/US_65th_Infantry_Regiment.Painting.Korean_War.Bayonet_charge_against_Chinese_division.jpg/420px-US_65th_Infantry_Regiment.Painting.Korean_War.Bayonet_charge_against_Chinese_division.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/US_65th_Infantry_Regiment.Painting.Korean_War.Bayonet_charge_against_Chinese_division.jpg/560px-US_65th_Infantry_Regiment.Painting.Korean_War.Bayonet_charge_against_Chinese_division.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_65th_Infantry_Regiment.Painting.Korean_War.Bayonet_charge_against_Chinese_division.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Painting of bayonet charge by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._65th_Infantry_Regiment" title="U.S. 65th Infantry Regiment">U.S. 65th Infantry Regiment</a>, made up of Puerto Rican troops, against a Chinese division during the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A bill was introduced before the Puerto Rican Senate which would restrain the rights of the independence and nationalist movements in the island. The Senate at the time was controlled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">Popular Democratic Party</a> (PPD), and was presided over by Luis Muñoz Marín.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[79]</a></sup> The bill, also known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico%27s_Gag_Law" title="Puerto Rico's Gag Law">Gag Law</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i>Ley de la Mordaza</i></span>), was approved by the legislature on May 21, 1948. It made it illegal to display a Puerto Rican flag, to sing a pro-independence tune, to talk of independence, or to campaign for independence.</p>
<p>The bill, which resembled <a href="/wiki/Smith_Act" title="Smith Act">the Smith Act passed in the United States</a>, was signed and made into law on June 10, 1948, by the U.S. appointed governor of Puerto Rico, <a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_T._Pi%C3%B1ero" title="Jesús T. Piñero">Jesús T. Piñero</a>, and became known as "Law 53" (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i>Ley 53</i></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[l]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In accordance with this law, it would be a crime to print, publish, sell, exhibit, organize or help anyone organize any society, group or assembly of people whose intentions are to paralyze or destroy the insular government. Anyone accused and found guilty of disobeying the law could be sentenced to ten years of prison, be fined $10,000 (US), or both. According to Dr. <a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_Figueroa" title="Leopoldo Figueroa">Leopoldo Figueroa</a>, a member of the Puerto Rico House of Representatives, the law was repressive and in violation of the First Amendment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Constitution" title="US Constitution">US Constitution</a>, which guarantees <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_of_Speech" title="Freedom of Speech">Freedom of Speech</a>. He asserted that the law as such was a violation of the civil rights of the people of Puerto Rico. The law was repealed in 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LG_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-LG-94">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1950, the U.S. Congress approved Public Law 600 (P.L. 81-600), which allowed for a democratic <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> in Puerto Rico to determine whether Puerto Ricans desired to draft their own local constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[83]</a></sup> This Act was meant to be adopted in the "nature of a compact". It required congressional approval of the Puerto Rico Constitution before it could go into effect, and repealed certain sections of the Organic Act of 1917. The sections of this statute left in force were entitled the <i>Puerto Rican Federal Relations Act</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-View_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-View-96">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[85]</a></sup> U.S. Secretary of the Interior <a href="/wiki/Oscar_L._Chapman" title="Oscar L. Chapman">Oscar L. Chapman</a>, under whose Department resided responsibility of Puerto Rican affairs, clarified the new commonwealth status in this manner:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The bill (to permit Puerto Rico to write its own constitution) merely authorizes the people of Puerto Rico to adopt their own constitution and to organize a local government...The bill under consideration would not change Puerto Rico's political, social, and economic relationship to the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[87]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em">
<caption>External video</caption>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aguadilla_Pueblo.jpg"><img alt="Aguadilla Pueblo.jpg" data-file-height="961" data-file-width="1519" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Aguadilla_Pueblo.jpg/210px-Aguadilla_Pueblo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Aguadilla_Pueblo.jpg/315px-Aguadilla_Pueblo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Aguadilla_Pueblo.jpg/420px-Aguadilla_Pueblo.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" width="16"/> <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_71hkXrTTf8" rel="nofollow">Puerto Rico</a>, U.S. Embassy in Vienna, October 24, 2014</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" width="16"/> View newsreel scenes in Spanish of the <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RfOJj0nmGEU" rel="nofollow"><span class="plainlinks"><i>Puerto Rican Nationalist Party Revolts of the 1950s</i></span></a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On October 30, 1950, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Albizu_Campos" title="Pedro Albizu Campos">Pedro Albizu Campos</a> and other nationalists led a three-day revolt against the United States in various cities and towns of Puerto Rico, in what is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Nationalist_Party_Revolts_of_the_1950s" title="Puerto Rican Nationalist Party Revolts of the 1950s">Puerto Rican Nationalist Party Revolts of the 1950s</a>. The most notable occurred in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jayuya" title="Jayuya">Jayuya</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utuado" title="Utuado">Utuado</a>. In the Jayuya revolt, known as the <a href="/wiki/Jayuya_Uprising" title="Jayuya Uprising">Jayuya Uprising</a>, the Puerto Rican governor declared <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">martial law</a>, and attacked the insurgents in Jayuya with infantry, artillery and bombers under control of the Puerto Rican commander. The <a href="/wiki/Utuado_uprising" title="Utuado uprising">Utuado uprising</a> culminated in what is known as the Utuado massacre.</p>
<p>On November 1, 1950, Puerto Rican nationalists from New York City, <a href="/wiki/Griselio_Torresola" title="Griselio Torresola">Griselio Torresola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Collazo" title="Oscar Collazo">Oscar Collazo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Truman_assassination_attempt" title="Truman assassination attempt">attempted to assassinate</a> President <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a> at his temporary residence of Blair House. Torresola was killed during the attack, but Collazo was wounded and captured. He was convicted of murder and sentenced to death, but President Truman commuted his sentence to life. After Collazo served 29 years in a federal prison, President Jimmy Carter commuted his sentence to times served and he was released in 1979.</p>
<p>Pedro Albizu Campos served many years in a federal prison in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, for seditious conspiracy to overthrow the U.S. government in Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Constitution of Puerto Rico">Constitution of Puerto Rico</a> was approved by a Constitutional Convention on February 6, 1952, and 82% of the voters in a March referendum. It was modified and ratified by the U.S. Congress, approved by President Truman on July 3 of that year, and proclaimed by Gov. Muñoz Marín on July 25, 1952. This was the anniversary of July 25, 1898, landing of U.S. troops in the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Campaign" title="Puerto Rican Campaign">Puerto Rican Campaign</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, until then celebrated as an annual Puerto Rico holiday.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:297px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546368.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2040" data-file-width="3000" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546368.jpg/295px-MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546368.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546368.jpg/443px-MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546368.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546368.jpg/590px-MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546368.jpg 2x" width="295"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546368.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shantytown" title="Shantytown">shantytown</a> along the Martin Peña Channel (1973)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Puerto Rico adopted the name of <i><a href="/wiki/Estado_Libre_Asociado_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Estado Libre Asociado de Puerto Rico">Estado Libre Asociado de Puerto Rico</a></i> (literally "Associated Free State of Puerto Rico"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[89]</a></sup>), officially translated into English as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(United_States_insular_area)" title="Commonwealth (United States insular area)">Commonwealth</a>, for its <a href="/wiki/Body_politic" title="Body politic">body politic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[m]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[91]</a></sup> "The United States Congress legislates over many fundamental aspects of Puerto Rican life, including citizenship, the currency, the postal service, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a>, military defense, communications, <a href="/wiki/Labor_relations" title="Labor relations">labor relations</a>, the environment, commerce, finance, health and welfare, and many others."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-105">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1950s and 1960s, Puerto Rico experienced rapid industrialization, due in large part to <i>Operación Manos a la Obra</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Operation_Bootstrap" title="Operation Bootstrap">Operation Bootstrap</a>"), an offshoot of FDR's New Deal. It was intended to transform Puerto Rico's economy from agriculture-based to manufacturing-based to provide more jobs. Puerto Rico has become a major tourist destination, as well as a global center for pharmaceutical manufacturing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pharma_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-pharma-106">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plebiscites_on_statehood_or_independence">Plebiscites on statehood or independence</span></h3>
<p>Four plebiscites have been held since the late 20th century to resolve the political status. The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_status_referendum,_2012" title="Puerto Rican status referendum, 2012">2012 referendum</a> showed a majority (54% of the voters) in favor of a change in status, with full statehood the preferred option of those who wanted a change. Because there were almost 500,000 blank ballots in the 2012 referendum, creating confusion as to the voters' true desire, Congress decided to ignore the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first three plebiscites provided voters with three options: statehood, free association, and independence. The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_status_referendum,_2017" title="Puerto Rican status referendum, 2017">Puerto Rican status referendum, 2017</a> in June 2017 was going to offer only two options: Statehood and Independence/Free Association. However, a letter from the <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> administration recommended adding the Commonwealth, the current status, in the plebiscite. The option had been removed from this plebiscite in response to the results of the plebiscite in 2012 which asked whether to remain in the current status and No had won. The Trump administration cited changes in demographics during the past 5 years to add the option once again. Amendments to the plebiscite bill were adopted making ballot wording changes requested by the Department of Justice, as well as adding a "current territorial status" option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[96]</a></sup> While 97 percent voted in favor of statehood, the turnout was low; only some 23 percent voted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[97]</a></sup> After the ballots were counted the Justice Department was non-committal. The Justice Department had asked for the 2017 plebiscite to be postponed but the Rosselló government chose not to do so. After the outcome was announced, the department told the Associated Press that it had "not reviewed or approved the ballot’s language".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>Former Governor <a href="/wiki/An%C3%ADbal_Acevedo_Vil%C3%A1" title="Aníbal Acevedo Vilá">Aníbal Acevedo Vilá</a> (2005–2009) is convinced that statehood is not the solution for either the U.S. or for Puerto Rico "for economic, identity and cultural reasons". He pointed out that voter turnout for the 2017 referendum was extremely low, and suggests that a different type of mutually-beneficial relationship should be found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[99]</a></sup></p>
