<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bomba-1.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A dancer performs typical <i><a href="/wiki/Bomba_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Bomba (Puerto Rico)">bomba</a></i> choreography.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The music of Puerto Rico has evolved as a heterogeneous and dynamic product of diverse cultural resources. The most conspicuous musical sources have been Spain and West Africa, although many aspects of Puerto Rican music reflect origins elsewhere in Europe and the Caribbean and, over the last century, from the U.S. Puerto Rican music culture today comprises a wide and rich variety of genres, ranging from indigenous genres like <a href="/wiki/Bomba_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Bomba (Puerto Rico)">bomba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plena" title="Plena">plena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aguinaldo" title="Aguinaldo">aguinaldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danza" title="Danza">danza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">salsa</a> to recent hybrids like <a href="/wiki/Reggaeton" title="Reggaeton">reggaeton</a>.</p>
<p>Puerto Rico has some national instruments, like the Cuatro (Spanish for Four). The cuatro is a local instrument that was made by the "Jibaro" or people from the mountains. Originally, the Cuatro consisted of four steel strings, hence its name, but currently the Cuatro consists of five double steel strings. It is easily confused with a guitar, even by locals. When held upright, from right to left, the strings are G, D, A, E, B.</p>
<p>In the realm of <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a>, the island hosts two main orchestras, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orquesta_Sinf%C3%B3nica_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Orquesta Sinfónica de Puerto Rico">Orquesta Sinfónica de Puerto Rico</a> and the Orquesta Filarmónica de Puerto Rico. The <a href="/wiki/Casals_Festival" title="Casals Festival">Casals Festival</a> takes place annually in San Juan, drawing in classical musicians from around the world.</p>
<p>With respect to <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, the legendary Puerto Rican tenor <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Paoli" title="Antonio Paoli">Antonio Paoli</a> was so celebrated, that he performed private recitals for <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_X" title="Pope Pius X">Pope Pius X</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czar_Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Czar Nicholas II of Russia">Czar Nicholas II of Russia</a>. In 1907, Paoli was the first operatic artist in world history to record an entire opera – when he participated in a performance of <i><a href="/wiki/Pagliacci" title="Pagliacci">Pagliacci</a></i> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruggiero_Leoncavallo" title="Ruggiero Leoncavallo">Ruggiero Leoncavallo</a> in Milan, Italy.</p>
<p>Over the past fifty years, Puerto Rican artists such as Jorge Emmanuelli, <a href="/wiki/Yomo_Toro" title="Yomo Toro">Yomo Toro</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramito" title="Ramito">Ramito</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_Feliciano" title="Jose Feliciano">Jose Feliciano</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bobby_Capo" title="Bobby Capo">Bobby Capo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Cortijo" title="Rafael Cortijo">Rafael Cortijo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ismael_Rivera" title="Ismael Rivera">Ismael Rivera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chayanne" title="Chayanne">Chayanne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tito_Puente" title="Tito Puente">Tito Puente</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Palmieri" title="Eddie Palmieri">Eddie Palmieri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ray_Barreto" title="Ray Barreto">Ray Barreto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Valentin" title="Dave Valentin">Dave Valentin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Rodr%C3%ADguez-L%C3%B3pez" title="Omar Rodríguez-López">Omar Rodríguez-López</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hector_Lavoe" title="Hector Lavoe">Hector Lavoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Anthony" title="Marc Anthony">Marc Anthony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Fonsi" title="Luis Fonsi">Luis Fonsi</a> have thrilled audiences around the world.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_cuisine" title="Puerto Rican cuisine">Puerto Rican cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuchifritos.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="345" data-file-width="385" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ef/Cuchifritos.jpg/215px-Cuchifritos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ef/Cuchifritos.jpg/323px-Cuchifritos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/ef/Cuchifritos.jpg 2x" width="215"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cuchifritos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Cuchifritos" title="Cuchifritos">Cuchifritos</a></i> (<i>Carnitas</i>) in New York</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Puerto Rican cuisine has its roots in the cooking traditions and practices of Europe (Spain), Africa and the native <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taínos</a>. In the latter part of the 19th century, the cuisine of Puerto Rico was greatly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_United_States" title="Cuisine of the United States">United States</a> in the ingredients used in its preparation. Puerto Rican cuisine has transcended the boundaries of the island, and can be found in several countries outside the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a>. Basic ingredients include <a href="/wiki/Grain" title="Grain">grains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herb" title="Herb">herbs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spices</a>, starchy tropical <a href="/wiki/Tuber" title="Tuber">tubers</a>, vegetables, meat and poultry, seafood and shellfish, and fruits. Main dishes include <i><a href="/wiki/Mofongo" title="Mofongo">mofongo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Arroz_con_gandules" title="Arroz con gandules">arroz con gandules</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pasteles" title="Pasteles">pasteles</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcapurrias" title="Alcapurrias">alcapurrias</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Pig_roast" title="Pig roast">pig roast</a> (or lechón). Beverages include <i><a href="/wiki/Mauby" title="Mauby">maví</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pi%C3%B1a_colada" title="Piña colada">piña colada</a></i>. Desserts include flan, <i>arroz con dulce</i> (sweet <a href="/wiki/Rice_pudding" title="Rice pudding">rice pudding</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Piragua_(food)" title="Piragua (food)">piraguas</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazo_gitano" title="Brazo gitano">brazo gitanos</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tembleque" title="Tembleque">tembleque</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Polvor%C3%B3n" title="Polvorón">polvorones</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Dulce_de_leche" title="Dulce de leche">dulce de leche</a></i>.</p>
<p>Locals call their cuisine <i><b>cocina criolla</b></i>. The traditional Puerto Rican cuisine was well established by the end of the 19th century. By 1848 the first restaurant, <a href="/wiki/La_Mallorquina" title="La Mallorquina">La Mallorquina</a>, opened in <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>. <i>El Cocinero Puertorriqueño</i>, the island's first cookbook was published in 1849.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-368"><a href="#cite_note-368">[338]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aranitas_tostones.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="424" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Aranitas_tostones.jpg/215px-Aranitas_tostones.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Aranitas_tostones.jpg/323px-Aranitas_tostones.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/Aranitas_tostones.jpg 2x" width="215"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aranitas_tostones.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Plantain "arañitas" and "tostones rellenos"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the diet of the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> people come many tropical roots and tubers like <i><a href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">yautía</a></i> (taro) and especially <i>Yuca</i> (cassava), from which thin cracker-like <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casabe" title="Casabe">casabe</a></i> bread is made. Ajicito or cachucha pepper, a slightly hot habanero pepper, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Culantro" title="Culantro">recao/culantro</a></i> (spiny leaf), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annato" title="Annato">achiote</a></i> (annatto), <i><a href="/wiki/Capsicum" title="Capsicum">peppers</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Aj%C3%AD_caballero" title="Ají caballero">ají caballero</a></i> (the hottest pepper native to Puerto Rico), peanuts, <a href="/wiki/Guava" title="Guava">guavas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapples</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cocoplum" title="Cocoplum">jicacos</a></i> (cocoplum), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mamoncillo" title="Mamoncillo">quenepas</a></i> (mamoncillo), <i><a href="/wiki/Calathea_allouia" title="Calathea allouia">lerenes</a></i> (Guinea arrowroot), <i><a href="/wiki/Calabaza" title="Calabaza">calabazas</a></i> (tropical pumpkins), and <i><a href="/wiki/Soursop" title="Soursop">guanabanas</a></i> (soursops) are all Taíno foods. The Taínos also grew varieties of <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a> and some maize/corn, but maize was not as dominant in their cooking as it was for the peoples living on the mainland of <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>. This is due to the frequent hurricanes that Puerto Rico experiences, which destroy crops of maize, leaving more safeguarded plants like <i>conucos</i> (hills of <i>yuca</i> grown together).</p>
<p>Spanish / European influence is also seen in Puerto Rican cuisine. Wheat, <a href="/wiki/Chickpea" title="Chickpea">chickpeas</a> (garbanzos), <a href="/wiki/Caper" title="Caper">capers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_pepper" title="Black pepper">black pepper</a>, onions, garlic, <i>cilantrillo</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cilantro" title="Cilantro">cilantro</a>), <a href="/wiki/Oregano" title="Oregano">oregano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basil" title="Basil">basil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a> fruit, <a href="/wiki/Eggplant" title="Eggplant">eggplant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ham" title="Ham">ham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lard" title="Lard">lard</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicken_(food)" title="Chicken (food)">chicken</a>, beef, pork, and cheese all came to Borikén (Puerto Rico's native Taino name) from Spain. The tradition of cooking complex stews and rice dishes in pots such as rice and beans are also thought to be originally European (much like Italians, Spaniards, and the British). Early <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>, French, Italian, and Chinese immigrants influenced not only the culture but Puerto Rican cooking as well. This great variety of traditions came together to form La Cocina Criolla.</p>
<p>Coconuts, coffee (brought by the Arabs and Corsos to Yauco from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaffa_Province,_Ethiopia" title="Kaffa Province, Ethiopia">Kafa</a>, Ethiopia), <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sesame_seeds" title="Sesame seeds">sesame seeds</a>, <i>gandules</i> (<a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon peas</a> in English) sweet bananas, plantains, other root vegetables and Guinea hen, all come to Puerto Rico from Africa.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philately">Philately</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_on_stamps" title="Puerto Rico on stamps">Puerto Rico on stamps</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Juan_1971_U.S._stamp.1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="289" data-file-width="184" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/San_Juan_1971_U.S._stamp.1.jpg/170px-San_Juan_1971_U.S._stamp.1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/San_Juan_1971_U.S._stamp.1.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Juan_1971_U.S._stamp.1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
San Juan 450th<br/>
1971 issue</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Puerto Rico has been commemorated on four U.S. postal stamps and four personalities have been featured. Insular Territories were commemorated in 1937, the third stamp honored Puerto Rico featuring '<a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>', the Spanish Governor's Palace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-369"><a href="#cite_note-369">[339]</a></sup> The first free election for governor of the US colony of Puerto Rico was honored on April 27, 1949, at San Juan, Puerto Rico. 'Inauguration' on the 3-cent stamp refers to the election of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luis_Munoz_Marin" title="Luis Munoz Marin">Luis Munoz Marin</a>, the first democratically elected governor of Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puerto_Rico_Election_Issue_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-Puerto_Rico_Election_Issue-370">[340]</a></sup> San Juan, Puerto Rico was commemorated with an 8-cent stamp on its 450th anniversary issued September 12, 1971, featuring a sentry box from <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">Castillo San Felipe del Morro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-371"><a href="#cite_note-371">[341]</a></sup> In the "Flags of our nation series" 2008–2012, of the fifty-five, five territorial flags were featured. Forever stamps included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flags_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Flags of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico Flag</a> illustrated by a bird issued 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-372"><a href="#cite_note-372">[342]</a></sup></p>
<p>Four Puerto Rican personalities have been featured on U.S. postage stamps. These include <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Clemente" title="Roberto Clemente">Roberto Clemente</a> in 1984 as an individual and in the Legends of Baseball series issued in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-373"><a href="#cite_note-373">[343]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn" title="Luis Muñoz Marín">Luis Muñoz Marín</a> in the Great Americans series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-374"><a href="#cite_note-374">[344]</a></sup> on February 18, 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puerto_Rico_Election_Issue_370-1"><a href="#cite_note-Puerto_Rico_Election_Issue-370">[340]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Julia_de_Burgos" title="Julia de Burgos">Julia de Burgos</a> in the Literary Arts series, issued 2010.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-375"><a href="#cite_note-375">[345]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ferrer" title="José Ferrer">José Ferrer</a> in the Distinguished American series, issued 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-376"><a href="#cite_note-376">[346]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Sports in Puerto Rico">Sports in Puerto Rico</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">Baseball</a> was one of the first sports to gain widespread popularity in Puerto Rico. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Baseball_League" title="Puerto Rico Baseball League">Puerto Rico Baseball League</a> serves as the only active professional league, operating as a winter league. No <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> franchise or affiliate plays in Puerto Rico, however, San Juan hosted the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a> for several series in 2003 and 2004 before they moved to Washington, D.C. and became the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_national_baseball_team" title="Puerto Rico national baseball team">Puerto Rico national baseball team</a> has participated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Cup_of_Baseball" title="World Cup of Baseball">World Cup of Baseball</a> winning one gold (1951), four silver and four bronze medals, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Series" title="Caribbean Series">Caribbean Series</a> (winning fourteen times) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic" title="World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classic</a>. On <span class="nowrap">March 2006</span>, San Juan's <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a> hosted the opening round as well as the second round of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic" title="World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classic</a>. Puerto Rican baseball players include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hall_of_Fame" title="Hall of Fame">Hall of Famers</a> <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Clemente" title="Roberto Clemente">Roberto Clemente</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Cepeda" title="Orlando Cepeda">Orlando Cepeda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Alomar" title="Roberto Alomar">Roberto Alomar</a>, enshrined in 1973, 1999, and 2011 respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-377"><a href="#cite_note-377">[347]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-378"><a href="#cite_note-378">[348]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-379"><a href="#cite_note-379">[349]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">Boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> are considered popular sports as well. <a href="/wiki/Wilfredo_G%C3%B3mez" title="Wilfredo Gómez">Wilfredo Gómez</a> and <a href="/wiki/McWilliams_Arroyo" title="McWilliams Arroyo">McWilliams Arroyo</a> have won their respective divisions at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Amateur_Boxing_Championships" title="World Amateur Boxing Championships">World Amateur Boxing Championships</a>. Other medalists include <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Pedraza_(boxer)" title="José Pedraza (boxer)">José Pedraza</a>, who holds a silver medal, and three boxers who finished in third place, José Luis Vellón, <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Dieppa" title="Nelson Dieppa">Nelson Dieppa</a> and <a href="/wiki/McJoe_Arroyo" title="McJoe Arroyo">McJoe Arroyo</a>. In the professional circuit, Puerto Rico has the third-most <a href="/wiki/List_of_Puerto_Rican_boxing_world_champions" title="List of Puerto Rican boxing world champions">boxing world champions</a> and it is the global leader in champions per capita. These include <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Cotto" title="Miguel Cotto">Miguel Cotto</a>, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Trinidad" title="Félix Trinidad">Félix Trinidad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Wilfred Benítez">Wilfred Benítez</a> and Gómez among others.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orangestarsultra.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Orangestarsultra.jpg/300px-Orangestarsultra.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Orangestarsultra.jpg/450px-Orangestarsultra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Orangestarsultra.jpg/600px-Orangestarsultra.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orangestarsultra.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Islanders" title="Puerto Rico Islanders">Puerto Rico Islanders</a> supporters' Orange Star Ultras at an association football game</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_national_basketball_team" title="Puerto Rico national basketball team">Puerto Rico national basketball team</a> joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Basketball_Federation" title="International Basketball Federation">International Basketball Federation</a> in 1957. Since then, it has won more than 30 medals in international competitions, including gold in three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIBA_Americas_Championship" title="FIBA Americas Championship">FIBA Americas Championships</a> and the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Goodwill_Games" title="Goodwill Games">Goodwill Games</a> August 8, 2004, became a landmark date for the team when it became the first team to defeat the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="United States men's national basketball team">United States</a> in an Olympic tournament since the integration of <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> players. Winning the inaugural game with scores of 92–73 as part of the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a> organized in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, Greece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-380"><a href="#cite_note-380">[350]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baloncesto_Superior_Nacional" title="Baloncesto Superior Nacional">Baloncesto Superior Nacional</a> acts as the top-level professional basketball league in Puerto Rico, and has experienced success since its beginning in 1930.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_national_football_team" title="Puerto Rico national football team">Puerto Rico</a> is also a member of <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> and <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a>. In 2008, the archipelago's first unified league, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Soccer_League" title="Puerto Rico Soccer League">Puerto Rico Soccer League</a>, was established.</p>
<p>Other sports include <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Road_running" title="Road running">road running</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_Wrestling_Council" title="World Wrestling Council">World Wrestling Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Wrestling_Association_(Puerto_Rico)" title="International Wrestling Association (Puerto Rico)">International Wrestling Association</a> are the largest wrestling promotions in the main island. The <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Best_10K" title="World's Best 10K">World's Best 10K</a>, held annually in San Juan, has been ranked among the 20 most competitive races globally. The "Puerto Rico All Stars" team, which has won twelve world championships in unicycle basketball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-381"><a href="#cite_note-381">[351]</a></sup></p>
<p>Organized <a href="/wiki/Streetball" title="Streetball">Streetball</a> has gathered some exposition, with teams like "Puerto Rico Street Ball" competing against established organizations including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arecibo_Captains" title="Arecibo Captains">Capitanes de Arecibo</a> and <a href="/wiki/AND1" title="AND1">AND1</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AND1_Mixtape_Tour" title="AND1 Mixtape Tour">Mixtape Tour Team</a>. Six years after the first visit, AND1 returned as part of their renamed Live Tour, losing to the Puerto Rico Streetballers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-382"><a href="#cite_note-382">[352]</a></sup> Consequently, practitioners of this style have earned participation in international teams, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orlando_Melendez" title="Orlando Melendez">Orlando "El Gato" Meléndez</a>, who became the first Puerto Rican born athlete to play for the <a href="/wiki/Harlem_Globetrotters" title="Harlem Globetrotters">Harlem Globetrotters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-383"><a href="#cite_note-383">[353]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Antigua" title="Orlando Antigua">Orlando Antigua</a>, whose mother is Puerto Rican, in 1995 became the first Hispanic and the first non-black in 52 years to play for the Harlem Globetrotters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-384"><a href="#cite_note-384">[354]</a></sup></p>
<p>Puerto Rico has representation in all international competitions including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" title="Summer Olympics">Summer</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_Olympics" title="Winter Olympics">Winter Olympics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_World_Series" title="Caribbean World Series">Caribbean World Series</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American and Caribbean Games</a>. Puerto Rico hosted the Pan Am Games in 1979 (officially in San Juan), and The <a href="/wiki/Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American and Caribbean Games</a> were hosted in <a href="/wiki/1993_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="1993 Central American and Caribbean Games">1993</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> and in <a href="/wiki/2010_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="2010 Central American and Caribbean Games">2010</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Mayagüez">Mayagüez</a>.</p>
<p>Puerto Rican athletes have won nine medals in Olympic competition (one gold, two silver, six bronze), the first one in 1948 by boxer <a href="/wiki/Juan_Evangelista_Venegas" title="Juan Evangelista Venegas">Juan Evangelista Venegas</a>. <a href="/wiki/Monica_Puig" title="Monica Puig">Monica Puig</a> won the first gold medal for Puerto Rico in the Olympic Games by winning the <a href="/wiki/Tennis_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics#Medal_events" title="Tennis at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Women's Tennis singles title in Rio 2016</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-385"><a href="#cite_note-385">[355]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-386"><a href="#cite_note-386">[356]</a></sup></p>

<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Puerto Rico" pronunciations: <span class="nowrap"><small>English:</small> <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɛər/: 'are' in 'bare'">ɛər</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Spanish: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[ˈpweɾto ˈriko]</a></span>, <small>rural,</small> <small>locally also </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ˈpwelto ˈχiko; ˈʀ̥iko]</a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Spanish word for commonwealth is typically <i><a href="/wiki/Mancomunidad" title="Mancomunidad">mancomunidad</a></i>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1932, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">U.S. Congress</a> officially back-corrected the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicization" title="Anglicization">Anglicization</a> of <i>Porto Rico</i> into the Spanish name <i>Puerto Rico</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> It had been using the former spelling in its legislative and judicial records since it acquired the territory. Patricia Gherovici states that both "Porto Rico" and "Puerto Rico" were used interchangeably in the news media and documentation before, during, and after the U.S. conquest of the island in 1898. The "Porto" spelling, for instance, was used in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris</a>, but "Puerto" was used by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> that same year. Nancy Morris clarifies that "a curious oversight in the drafting of the <a href="/wiki/Foraker_Act" title="Foraker Act">Foraker Act</a> caused the name of the island to be officially misspelled".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> However, Gervasio Luis Garcia traces the Anglicized spelling to a <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)">National Geographic</a></i> article from 1899, after which the spelling was kept by many agencies and entities because of the ethnic and linguistic pride of the English-speaking citizens of the American mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Proyecto Salón Hogar (in Spanish) "<span lang="es">Los españoles le cambiaron el nombre de Borikén a San Juan Bautista y a la capital le llamaron Ciudad de Puerto Rico. Con los años, Ciudad de Puerto Rico pasó a ser San Juan, y San Juan Bautista pasó a ser Puerto Rico.</span>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Today, Puerto Ricans are also known as Boricuas, or people from Borinquen.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vicente_Ya%C3%B1ez_Pinz%C3%B3n" title="Vicente Yañez Pinzón">Vicente Yañez Pinzón</a> is considered the first appointed governor of Puerto Rico, but he never arrived from Spain.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a>, to which they had no natural <a href="/wiki/Immunity_(medical)" title="Immunity (medical)">immunity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[45]</a></sup> For example, a <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> outbreak in 1518–1519 killed much of the Island's indigenous population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[46]</a></sup> "The first <i>repartimiento</i> in Puerto Rico is established, allowing colonists fixed numbers of Tainos for wage-free and forced labor in the gold mines. When several priests protest, the crown requires Spaniards to pay native laborers and to teach them the Christian religion; the colonists continue to treat the natives as slaves."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[47]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Tavenner (2010) "The Taíno people living [in Puerto Rico] at the time [...] were forced into slavery."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[48]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-58">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Poole (2011) "[The Taíno] began to starve; many thousands fell prey to smallpox, measles and other European diseases for which they had no immunity [...]"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[49]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-60">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a> "[The Taíno] eventually succumbed to the Spanish soldiers and European diseases that followed Columbus's arrival in the New World in 1492."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[50]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a> "[...] the high death rate among the Taíno due to enslavement and European diseases (smallpox, influenza, measles, and typhus) persisted."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[51]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-92">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cockcroft (2001; in Spanish) "[La Ley 53] fué llamada la 'pequeña ley Smith', debido a la semejanza con la Ley Smith de Estados Unidos [...]"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[80]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">However, as Robert William Anderson states on page 14 of his book "Party Politics in Puerto Rico" (Stanford, California: Stanford University Press. 1965.), <i>No one disputes the ambiguous status of the current Commonwealth. It is illustrated in the very different images conjured up by the English term "commonwealth" and the Spanish version, Estado Libre Asociado (literally, free associated state). The issue seems to be whether this ambiguity is a purposeful virtue or a disguised colonial vice.</i></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-229"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-229">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">pr.gov (in Spanish) "La manufactura es el sector principal de la economía de Puerto Rico."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manufacturing-by-pr.gov_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-manufacturing-by-pr.gov-228">[215]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-230"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-230">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">pr.gov (in Spanish) "Algunas de las industrias más destacadas dentro del sector de la manufactura son: las farmacéuticas, los textiles, los petroquímicos, las computadoras, la electrónica y las compañías dedicadas a la manufactura de instrumentos médicos y científicos, entre otros."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manufacturing-by-pr.gov_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-manufacturing-by-pr.gov-228">[215]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-234"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-234">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Torrech San Inocencio (2011; in Spanish) "Con los más de $1,500 millones anuales que recibimos en asistencia federal para alimentos podríamos desarrollar una industria alimentaria autosuficiente en Puerto Rico."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[218]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-236"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-236">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Millán Rodriguez (2013; in Spanish) "Los representantes del Pueblo en la Junta de Gobierno de la Autoridad de Energía Eléctrica [...] denunciaron ayer que la propuesta del Gobernador para hacer cambios en la composición del organismo institucionaliza la intervención político partidista en la corporación pública y la convierte en una agencia del Ejecutivo.."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[219]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-238"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-238">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vera Rosa (2013; in Spanish) "Aunque Puerto Rico mueve entre el sector público y privado $15 billones en el área de salud, las deficiencias en el sistema todavía no alcanzan un nivel de eficiencia óptimo."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-el-vocero-inefficient-health-2013_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-el-vocero-inefficient-health-2013-237">[220]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-239"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-239">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vera Rosado (2013; in Spanish) "Para mejorar la calidad de servicio, que se impacta principalmente por deficiencias administrativas y no por falta de dinero[...]"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-el-vocero-inefficient-health-2013_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-el-vocero-inefficient-health-2013-237">[220]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-241"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-241">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">González (2012; in Spanish) "[...] al analizarse la deuda pública de la Isla contra el Producto Interno Bruto (PIB), se ubicaría en una relación deuda/PIB de 68% aproximadamente."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[221]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-243"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-243">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bauzá (2013; in Spanish) "La realidad de nuestra situación económica y fiscal es resultado de años de falta de acción. Al Gobierno le faltó creatividad, innovación y rapidez en la creación de un nuevo modelo económico que sustentara nuestra economía. Tras la eliminación de la Sección 936, debimos ser proactivos, y no lo fuimos."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[222]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-245"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-245">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Quintero (2013; in Spanish) "Los indicadores de una economía débil son muchos, y la economía en Puerto Rico está sumamente debilitada, según lo evidencian la tasa de desempleo (13.5%), los altos niveles de pobreza (41.7%), los altos niveles de quiebra y la pérdida poblacional."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[223]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-260"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-260">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Walsh (2013) "In each of the last six years, Puerto Rico sold hundreds of millions of dollars of new bonds just to meet payments on its older, outstanding bonds – a red flag. It also sold $2.5 billion worth of bonds to raise cash for its troubled pension system – a risky practice – and it sold still more long-term bonds to cover its yearly budget deficits."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[237]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-263"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-263">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">PRGDB "Financial Information and Operating Data Report to October 18, 2013" p. 142<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gdb-report-2013_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-gdb-report-2013-262">[239]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-270"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-270">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">MRGI (2008) "Many female migrants leave their families behind due to the risk of illegal travel and the high cost of living in Puerto Rico."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refworld.org_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-refworld.org-269">[245]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-280"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-280">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Rivera. "Housing prices in Puerto Rico are comparable to Miami or Los Angeles, but property taxes are considerably lower than most places in the US."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[254]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-283"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-283">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">FRBNY (2011) "...home values vary considerably across municipios: for the metro area overall, the median value of owner-occupied homes was estimated at $126,000 (based on data for 2007–09), but these medians ranged from $214,000 in Guaynabo to around $100,000 in some of the outlying municipios. The median value in the San Juan municipio was estimated at $170,000."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[256]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-286"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-286">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Santiago (2021) "Local detractors of the Jones Act [...] for many years have unsuccessfully tried to have Puerto Rico excluded from the law's provisions[...]"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[258]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-joc-gao-report-repeal-quote-290"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-joc-gao-report-repeal-quote_290-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">JOC (2013) "Repealing or amending the Jones Act cabotage law might cut Puerto Rico shipping costs"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joc-gao-report_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-joc-gao-report-289">[261]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-joc-gao-report-lower-costs-quote-291"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-joc-gao-report-lower-costs-quote_291-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">JOC (2013) "The GAO report said its interviews with shippers indicated they [...] believed that opening the trade to non-U.S.-flag competition could lower costs."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joc-gao-report_289-1"><a href="#cite_note-joc-gao-report-289">[261]</a></sup></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://ballotpedia.org/Puerto_Rico_Statehood,_Independence,_or_Free_Association_Referendum_(2017)" rel="nofollow">"Puerto Rico Statehood, Independence, or Free Association Referendum (2017)"</a>. <i>Ballotpedia</i>. BALLOTPEDIA. February 6, 2017<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">February 24,</span> 2017</span>. <q>With my vote, I make the initial request to the Federal Government to begin the process of the decolonization through: (1) Free Association: Puerto Rico should adopt a status outside of the Territory Clause of the Constitution of the United States that recognizes the sovereignty of the People of Puerto Rico. The Free Association would be based on a free and voluntary political association, the specific terms of which shall be agreed upon between the United States and Puerto Rico as sovereign nations. Such agreement would provide the scope of the jurisdictional powers that the People of Puerto Rico agree to confer to the United States and retain all other jurisdictional powers and authorities. Under this option the American citizenship would be subject to negotiation with the United States Government; (2) Proclamation of Independence, I demand that the United States Government, in the exercise of its power to dispose of territory, recognize the national sovereignty of Puerto Rico as a completely independent nation and that the United States Congress enact the necessary legislation to initiate the negotiation and transition to the independent nation of Puerto Rico. My vote for Independence also represents my claim to the rights, duties, powers, and prerogatives of independent and democratic republics, my support of Puerto Rican citizenship, and a "Treaty of Friendship and Cooperation" between Puerto Rico and the United States after the transition process</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APuerto+Rico&amp;rft.atitle=Puerto+Rico+Statehood%2C+Independence%2C+or+Free+Association+Referendum+%282017%29&amp;rft.date=2017-02-06&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Ballotpedia&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fballotpedia.org%2FPuerto_Rico_Statehood%2C_Independence%2C_or_Free_Association_Referendum_%282017%29&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-174"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-174">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Downes_v._Bidwell" title="Downes v. Bidwell">Downes v. Bidwell</a>, 182 U.S. 244, 261 (1901), commenting on an earlier Supreme Court decision, Loughborough v. Blake, 18 U.S. (5 Wheat.) 317 (1820); Rasmussen v. United States, 197 U.S. 516, 529–530, 536 (1905)(concurring opinions of Justices Harlan and Brown), that once the Constitution has been extended to an area, its coverage is irrevocable; <a href="/wiki/Boumediene_v._Bush" title="Boumediene v. Bush">Boumediene v. Bush</a> – That where the Constitution has been once formally extended by Congress to territories, neither Congress nor the territorial legislature can enact laws inconsistent therewith. The Constitution grants Congress and the President the power to acquire, dispose of, and govern territory, not the power to decide when and where its terms apply.</span></li>
